Afghanistan map of <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Afghanistan_physical_en.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1624" data-file-width="2079" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Afghanistan_physical_en.png/220px-Afghanistan_physical_en.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Afghanistan_physical_en.png/330px-Afghanistan_physical_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Afghanistan_physical_en.png/440px-Afghanistan_physical_en.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Afghanistan_physical_en.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Topography</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landlocked" title="Landlocked">landlocked</a> mountainous country with plains in the north and southwest, Afghanistan is located within South Asia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-South_Asia_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-South_Asia-11">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNdata_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNdata-103">[102]</a></sup> and Central Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-104">[103]</a></sup> It is part of the US-coined <a href="/wiki/Greater_Middle_East" title="Greater Middle East">Greater Middle East</a> <a href="/wiki/Muslim_world" title="Muslim world">Muslim world</a>, which lies between <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitudes</a> <a href="/wiki/29th_parallel_north" title="29th parallel north"><span class="nowrap">29° N</span></a> and <a href="/wiki/39th_parallel_north" title="39th parallel north"><span class="nowrap">39° N</span></a>, and <a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">longitudes</a> <a href="/wiki/60th_meridian_east" title="60th meridian east"><span class="nowrap">60° E</span></a> and <a href="/wiki/75th_meridian_east" title="75th meridian east"><span class="nowrap">75° E</span></a>. The country's highest point is <a href="/wiki/Noshaq" title="Noshaq">Noshaq</a>, at 7,492 m (24,580 ft) above sea level. It has a <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental climate</a> with harsh winters in the <a href="/wiki/Hazarajat" title="Hazarajat">central highlands</a>, the glaciated northeast (around <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuristan" title="Nuristan">Nuristan</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Wakhan_Corridor" title="Wakhan Corridor">Wakhan Corridor</a>, where the average temperature in January is below −15 °C (5 °F), and hot summers in the low-lying areas of the <a href="/wiki/Sistan_Basin" title="Sistan Basin">Sistan Basin</a> of the southwest, the <a href="/wiki/Jalalabad" title="Jalalabad">Jalalabad</a> basin in the east, and the <a href="/wiki/Afghan_Turkestan" title="Afghan Turkestan">Turkestan</a> plains along the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amu_River" title="Amu River">Amu River</a> in the north, where temperatures average over 35 °C (95 °F) in July.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Geography_of_Afghanistan.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="690" data-file-width="1024" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Geography_of_Afghanistan.jpg/270px-Geography_of_Afghanistan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Geography_of_Afghanistan.jpg/405px-Geography_of_Afghanistan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Geography_of_Afghanistan.jpg/540px-Geography_of_Afghanistan.jpg 2x" width="270"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Geography_of_Afghanistan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Afghanistan" title="Geography of Afghanistan">Landscapes of Afghanistan</a>, from left to right: 1. <a href="/wiki/Band-e_Amir_National_Park" title="Band-e Amir National Park">Band-e Amir National Park</a>; 2. <a href="/wiki/Salang_Pass" title="Salang Pass">Salang Pass</a> in <a href="/wiki/Parwan_Province" title="Parwan Province">Parwan Province</a>; 3. <a href="/wiki/Korangal_Valley" title="Korangal Valley">Korangal Valley</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kunar_Province" title="Kunar Province">Kunar Province</a>; and 4. <a href="/wiki/Kajaki_Dam" title="Kajaki Dam">Kajaki Dam</a> in <a href="/wiki/Helmand_Province" title="Helmand Province">Helmand Province</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Despite having numerous rivers and <a href="/wiki/List_of_dams_and_reservoirs_in_Afghanistan" title="List of dams and reservoirs in Afghanistan">reservoirs</a>, large parts of the country are dry. The <a href="/wiki/Endorheic_basin" title="Endorheic basin">endorheic</a> Sistan Basin is one of the driest regions in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup> Aside from the usual rainfall, Afghanistan receives snow during the winter in the <a href="/wiki/Hindu_Kush" title="Hindu Kush">Hindu Kush</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pamir_Mountains" title="Pamir Mountains">Pamir Mountains</a>, and the melting snow in the spring season enters the <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_Afghanistan" title="List of rivers of Afghanistan">rivers, lakes, and streams</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> However, two-thirds of the country's water flows into the neighboring countries of Iran, Pakistan, and Turkmenistan. The state needs more than <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$2 billion</span> to rehabilitate its irrigation systems so that the water is properly managed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>The northeastern Hindu Kush <a href="/wiki/Mountain_range" title="Mountain range">mountain range</a>, in and around the <a href="/wiki/Badakhshan_Province" title="Badakhshan Province">Badakhshan Province</a> of Afghanistan, is in a <a href="/wiki/Natural_environment#Geological_activity" title="Natural environment">geologically active</a> area where earthquakes may occur almost every year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crone2007_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-crone2007-109">[108]</a></sup> They can be deadly and destructive sometimes, causing <a href="/wiki/Landslide" title="Landslide">landslides</a> in some parts or <a href="/wiki/2009_Afghan_avalanches" title="2009 Afghan avalanches">avalanches</a> during the winter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup> The last strong earthquakes were in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/February_4,_1998_Afghanistan_earthquake" title="February 4, 1998 Afghanistan earthquake">1998</a>, which killed about 6,000 people in Badakhshan near Tajikistan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbcquake2010_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbcquake2010-111">[110]</a></sup> This was followed by the <a href="/wiki/2002_Hindu_Kush_earthquakes" title="2002 Hindu Kush earthquakes">2002 Hindu Kush earthquakes</a> in which over 150 people were killed and over 1,000 injured. A <a href="/wiki/2010_Afghanistan_earthquake" title="2010 Afghanistan earthquake">2010 earthquake</a> left 11 Afghans dead, over 70 injured, and more than 2,000 houses destroyed.</p>
<p>The country's natural resources include: <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iron_ore" title="Iron ore">iron ore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lithium" title="Lithium">lithium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rare_earth_element" title="Rare earth element">rare earth elements</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chromite" title="Chromite">chromite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Talc" title="Talc">talc</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barites" title="Barites">barites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sulfur" title="Sulfur">sulfur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lead" title="Lead">lead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marble" title="Marble">marble</a>, precious and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi-precious_stones" title="Semi-precious stones">semi-precious stones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a>, among other things.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-peters2007_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-peters2007-112">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bgs_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-bgs-113">[112]</a></sup> In 2010, US and Afghan government officials estimated that untapped mineral deposits located in 2007 by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Geological_Survey" title="United States Geological Survey">US Geological Survey</a> are worth between <span class="nowrap">$900 bn</span> and <span class="nowrap">$3 trillion</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbcminerals_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbcminerals-114">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>At 652,230 km<sup>2</sup> (251,830 sq mi),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> Afghanistan is the world's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area">41st largest country</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> slightly bigger than France and smaller than Burma, about the size of Texas in the United States. It borders Pakistan in the south and east; Iran in the west; Turkmenistan, Uzbekistan, and Tajikistan in the north; and China in the far east.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Afghanistan" title="Demographics of Afghanistan">Demographics of Afghanistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Afghan_diaspora" title="Afghan diaspora">Afghan diaspora</a></div>
<p>As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Afghanistan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the population of Afghanistan is around 32,564,342,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Factbook_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Factbook-10">[9]</a></sup> which includes the roughly 2.7 million <a href="/wiki/Afghan_diaspora" title="Afghan diaspora">Afghan refugees</a> still living in <a href="/wiki/Afghans_in_Pakistan" title="Afghans in Pakistan">Pakistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Afghans_in_Iran" title="Afghans in Iran">Iran</a>. As of 2013 46% of Afghanistan's population are under 15 years of age and 74% of the population live in rural areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uis.unesco.org_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-uis.unesco.org-117">[116]</a></sup> The average woman gave birth to five children during her life and 6.8% of all babies died in child-birth or infancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uis.unesco.org_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-uis.unesco.org-117">[116]</a></sup> Life expectancy in 2013 was 60 years and only .1% of the population between ages 15 and 49 had <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uis.unesco.org_117-2"><a href="#cite_note-uis.unesco.org-117">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>Like many of its neighboring countries, Afghanistan has an ethnically, linguistically and religiously diverse population. According to cartographer <a href="/wiki/Mehrdad_Izady" title="Mehrdad Izady">Michael Izady</a> there "is precious little correspondence between language and ethnic or group identity in Afghanistan. Connections such as tribe (e.g. Pashtuns, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aimaqs" title="Aimaqs">Aimaqs</a>), religion (e.g. the Shia Hazaras, Sayyids, <a href="/wiki/Qizilbash#Afghanistan" title="Qizilbash">Kizilbash</a>), group memory (e.g. Arabs and Monghols/Mongols) or life style (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Farsiwan" title="Farsiwan">Parsiwans</a>) are far more important markers of group identity than language has ever been. Only Turkmens (totally) and Uzbeks (mostly) are to be identified with languages that they speak. This has been so since the inception of the state in AD 1747."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>Afghanistan has experienced a gradual <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">urbanization</a> since the late 1990s but the country remains one of the world's least urban societies. In 1999 around 79% of the country's population lived in rural areas compared to around 74% in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uis.unesco.org_117-3"><a href="#cite_note-uis.unesco.org-117">[116]</a></sup> The only city with over a million residents is its capital, Kabul. Other <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Afghanistan" title="List of cities in Afghanistan">large cities in the country</a> are, in order of population size, <a href="/wiki/Kandahar" title="Kandahar">Kandahar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herat" title="Herat">Herat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mazar-i-Sharif" title="Mazar-i-Sharif">Mazar-i-Sharif</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kunduz" title="Kunduz">Kunduz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jalalabad" title="Jalalabad">Jalalabad</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lashkar_Gah" title="Lashkar Gah">Lashkar Gah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taloqan" title="Taloqan">Taloqan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khost" title="Khost">Khost</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheberghan" title="Sheberghan">Sheberghan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ghazni" title="Ghazni">Ghazni</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/Population_Reference_Bureau" title="Population Reference Bureau">Population Reference Bureau</a>, the Afghan population is estimated to increase to 82 million by 2050.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Afghanistan" title="Ethnic groups in Afghanistan">Ethnic groups in Afghanistan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Army_ethnolinguistic_map_of_Afghanistan_--_circa_2001-09.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2123" data-file-width="2319" height="229" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/US_Army_ethnolinguistic_map_of_Afghanistan_--_circa_2001-09.jpg/250px-US_Army_ethnolinguistic_map_of_Afghanistan_--_circa_2001-09.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/US_Army_ethnolinguistic_map_of_Afghanistan_--_circa_2001-09.jpg/375px-US_Army_ethnolinguistic_map_of_Afghanistan_--_circa_2001-09.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/US_Army_ethnolinguistic_map_of_Afghanistan_--_circa_2001-09.jpg/500px-US_Army_ethnolinguistic_map_of_Afghanistan_--_circa_2001-09.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Army_ethnolinguistic_map_of_Afghanistan_--_circa_2001-09.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ethnolinguistics" title="Ethnolinguistics">Ethnolinguistic</a> groups of Afghanistan</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Afghanistan is a multiethnic society, and its historical status as a crossroads has contributed significantly to its diverse ethnic makeup. The population of the country is divided into a wide variety of <a href="/wiki/Ethnolinguistics" title="Ethnolinguistics">ethnolinguistic</a> groups. Because a systematic census has not been held in the nation in decades, exact figures about the size and composition of the various ethnic groups are unavailable. An approximate distribution of the ethnic groups is shown in the chart below:</p>

</div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pashto_language" title="Pashto language">Pashto</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dari_language" title="Dari language">Dari</a> are the <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official languages</a> of Afghanistan; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bilingualism" title="Bilingualism">bilingualism</a> is very common.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AO_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-AO-1">[1]</a></sup> Both are <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European languages</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_languages" title="Iranian languages">Iranian languages</a> sub-family. Dari (Afghan Persian) has long been the <a href="/wiki/Prestige_(sociolinguistics)" title="Prestige (sociolinguistics)">prestige language</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> for inter-ethnic communication. It is the native tongue of the Tajiks, Hazaras, Aimaks, and Kizilbash.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encyclop.C3.A6dia_Britannica_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclop.C3.A6dia_Britannica-126">[125]</a></sup> Pashto is the native tongue of the Pashtuns, although many Pashtuns often use Dari and some non-Pashtuns are fluent in Pashto.</p>
<p>Other languages, including <a href="/wiki/Uzbek_language" title="Uzbek language">Uzbek</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkmen_language" title="Turkmen language">Turkmen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Balochi_language" title="Balochi language">Balochi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pashayi_language" title="Pashayi language">Pashayi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nuristani_languages" title="Nuristani languages">Nuristani languages</a> (<a href="/wiki/Askunu_language" title="Askunu language">Ashkunu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kamkata-viri_language" title="Kamkata-viri language">Kamkata-viri</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vasi-vari_language" title="Vasi-vari language">Vasi-vari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tregami_language" title="Tregami language">Tregami</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kalasha-ala_language" title="Kalasha-ala language">Kalasha-ala</a>), are the native tongues of minority groups across the country and have official status in the regions where they are widely spoken. Minor languages also include <a href="/wiki/Pamir_languages" title="Pamir languages">Pamiri</a> (<a href="/wiki/Shughni_language" title="Shughni language">Shughni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Munji_language" title="Munji language">Munji</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ishkashimi_language" title="Ishkashimi language">Ishkashimi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wakhi_language" title="Wakhi language">Wakhi</a>), <a href="/wiki/Brahui_language" title="Brahui language">Brahui</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindko_language" title="Hindko language">Hindko</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_language" title="Kyrgyz language">Kyrgyz</a>. A small percentage of Afghans are also fluent in <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a>, English, and other languages.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gender">Gender</span></h3>
<p>Afghanistan was listed in 2002 as one of the most dangerous countries in the world to be born a woman according to a global survey due to some of the highest maternal mortality rates in the world, where half a million die annually in childbirth. The high rate is caused by the healthcare system having been destroyed by warfare and the Taliban.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unicef_6nov2002_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-unicef_6nov2002-127">[126]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religions">Religions</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Afghanistan" title="Religion in Afghanistan">Religion in Afghanistan</a></div>
<div class="barbox tright" style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">
<table style="border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">
<tr style="background:#ddd">

</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni Islam</a></td>
<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
<div style="background:green; width:70.0%; overflow: hidden;">  </div>

<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imamiyyah" title="Imamiyyah">Imamiyyah</a></td>

<div style="background:lightgreen; width:25.0%; overflow: hidden;">  </div>
</td>
<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">25.0%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Isma%27ilism" title="Isma'ilism">Ismāʿīlism</a></td>
<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
<div style="background:greenyellow; width:4.5%; overflow: hidden;">  </div>
</td>
<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">4.5%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Other religion</td>
<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
<div style="background:orange; width:0.5%; overflow: hidden;">  </div>
</td>
<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">0.5%</td>
</tr>
</table>
</div>
<p>Over 99% of the Afghan population is Muslim; up to 90% are from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunni" title="Sunni">Sunni</a> branch, 7–19% are <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam_in_Afghanistan" title="Shia Islam in Afghanistan">Shia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Factbook_10-3"><a href="#cite_note-Factbook-10">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LoC-pdf_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-LoC-pdf-23">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pew_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pew-129">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>Until the 1890s, the region around <a href="/wiki/Nuristan_Province" title="Nuristan Province">Nuristan</a> was known as <a href="/wiki/Kafiristan" title="Kafiristan">Kafiristan</a> (land of the <a href="/wiki/Kafir" title="Kafir">kafirs</a> (unbelievers)) because of its non-Muslim inhabitants, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuristani_people" title="Nuristani people">Nuristanis</a>, an ethnically distinct people whose religious practices included <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">animism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polytheism" title="Polytheism">polytheism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shamanism" title="Shamanism">shamanism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup> Thousands of Afghan <a href="/wiki/Sikhism_in_Afghanistan" title="Sikhism in Afghanistan">Sikhs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Afghanistan" title="Hinduism in Afghanistan">Hindus</a> are also found in the major cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup> There was a small <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Afghanistan" title="History of the Jews in Afghanistan">Jewish community in Afghanistan</a> who had emigrated to Israel and the United States by the end of the twentieth century; only one Jew, <a href="/wiki/Zablon_Simintov" title="Zablon Simintov">Zablon Simintov</a>, remained by 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Afghanistan" title="Politics of Afghanistan">Politics of Afghanistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Hamid_Karzai" title="Presidency of Hamid Karzai">Presidency of Hamid Karzai</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Afghanistan" title="Constitution of Afghanistan">Constitution of Afghanistan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Afghan_parliament_in_2006.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2016" data-file-width="3024" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Afghan_parliament_in_2006.jpg/220px-Afghan_parliament_in_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Afghan_parliament_in_2006.jpg/330px-Afghan_parliament_in_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Afghan_parliament_in_2006.jpg/440px-Afghan_parliament_in_2006.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Afghan_parliament_in_2006.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Afghanistan" title="National Assembly of Afghanistan">National Assembly of Afghanistan</a> in 2006</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taliban_insurgency_in_Afghanistan_(2015%E2%80%93present).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1331" data-file-width="1807" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Taliban_insurgency_in_Afghanistan_%282015%E2%80%93present%29.svg/220px-Taliban_insurgency_in_Afghanistan_%282015%E2%80%93present%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Taliban_insurgency_in_Afghanistan_%282015%E2%80%93present%29.svg/330px-Taliban_insurgency_in_Afghanistan_%282015%E2%80%93present%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Taliban_insurgency_in_Afghanistan_%282015%E2%80%93present%29.svg/440px-Taliban_insurgency_in_Afghanistan_%282015%E2%80%93present%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Taliban_insurgency_in_Afghanistan_(2015%E2%80%93present).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Current military situation, as of 27 February 2016.
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ebc0b3; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Under control of the <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Afghanistan" title="Politics of Afghanistan">Afghan Government</a>, <a href="/wiki/Resolute_Support_Mission" title="Resolute Support Mission">NATO</a>, and <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2015%E2%80%93present)#Allied_militias" title="War in Afghanistan (2015–present)">Allies</a></div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ffffff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Under control of the <a href="/wiki/Taliban" title="Taliban">Taliban</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">Al-Qaeda</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Jihad_Union" title="Islamic Jihad Union">Allies</a></div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #b3b2ae; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Under control of the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">Islamic State</a></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Afghanistan is an <a href="/wiki/Islamic_republic" title="Islamic republic">Islamic republic</a> consisting of three branches, the executive, legislative, and judicial. The nation is led by President <a href="/wiki/Ashraf_Ghani" title="Ashraf Ghani">Ashraf Ghani</a> with <a href="/wiki/Abdul_Rashid_Dostum" title="Abdul Rashid Dostum">Abdul Rashid Dostum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sarwar_Danish" title="Sarwar Danish">Sarwar Danish</a> as vice presidents. <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_Abdullah" title="Abdullah Abdullah">Abdullah Abdullah</a> serves as the chief executive officer (CEO). The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Afghanistan" title="National Assembly of Afghanistan">National Assembly</a> is the legislature, a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> body having two chambers, the <a href="/wiki/House_of_the_People_(Afghanistan)" title="House of the People (Afghanistan)">House of the People</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/House_of_Elders" title="House of Elders">House of Elders</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afghan_Supreme_Court" title="Afghan Supreme Court">Supreme Court</a> is led by <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_Afghanistan" title="Chief Justice of Afghanistan">Chief Justice</a> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Said_Yusuf_Halem&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Said Yusuf Halem (page does not exist)">Said Yusuf Halem</a>, the former Deputy Minister of Justice for Legal Affairs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup></p>
<p>A January 2010 report published by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_on_Drugs_and_Crime" title="United Nations Office on Drugs and Crime">United Nations Office on Drugs and Crime</a> revealed that bribery consumed an amount equal to 23% of the GDP of the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup> A number of <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_(Afghanistan)" title="Council of Ministers (Afghanistan)">government ministries</a> are believed to be rife with corruption, and while President Karzai vowed to tackle the problem in late 2009 by stating that "individuals who are involved in corruption will have no place in the government",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup> top government officials were stealing and misusing hundreds of millions of dollars through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kabul_Bank" title="Kabul Bank">Kabul Bank</a>. According to <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a>'s 2014 corruption perceptions index results, Afghanistan was ranked as the fourth most corrupt country in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TI_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-TI-138">[137]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elections_and_parties">Elections and parties</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Afghanistan" title="Elections in Afghanistan">Elections in Afghanistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Afghanistan" title="List of political parties in Afghanistan">List of political parties in Afghanistan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_meets_Abdullah_and_Ghani_2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1735" data-file-width="2614" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Secretary_Kerry_meets_Abdullah_and_Ghani_2014.jpg/220px-Secretary_Kerry_meets_Abdullah_and_Ghani_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Secretary_Kerry_meets_Abdullah_and_Ghani_2014.jpg/330px-Secretary_Kerry_meets_Abdullah_and_Ghani_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Secretary_Kerry_meets_Abdullah_and_Ghani_2014.jpg/440px-Secretary_Kerry_meets_Abdullah_and_Ghani_2014.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_meets_Abdullah_and_Ghani_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
From left to right: <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_Abdullah" title="Abdullah Abdullah">Abdullah Abdullah</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ashraf_Ghani" title="Ashraf Ghani">Ashraf Ghani</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Afghan_presidential_election,_2014" title="Afghan presidential election, 2014">2014 presidential election</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Afghan_presidential_election,_2004" title="Afghan presidential election, 2004">2004 Afghan presidential election</a> was relatively peaceful, in which Hamid Karzai won in the first round with 55.4% of the votes. However, the <a href="/wiki/Afghan_presidential_election,_2009" title="Afghan presidential election, 2009">2009 presidential election</a> was characterized by lack of security, low voter turnout, and widespread electoral fraud.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karzai_Gets_New_Term_as_Afghan_Runoff_is_Scrapped_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-Karzai_Gets_New_Term_as_Afghan_Runoff_is_Scrapped-139">[138]</a></sup> The vote, along with elections for 420 <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Afghanistan" title="Provinces of Afghanistan">provincial council</a> seats, took place in August 2009, but remained unresolved during a lengthy period of vote counting and fraud investigation.</p>
<p>Two months later, under international pressure, a second round run-off vote between Karzai and remaining challenger <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_Abdullah" title="Abdullah Abdullah">Abdullah</a> was announced, but a few days later Abdullah announced that he would not participate in 7 November run-off because his demands for changes in the electoral commission had not been met. The next day, officials of the election commission cancelled the run-off and declared Hamid Karzai as President for another five-year term.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karzai_Gets_New_Term_as_Afghan_Runoff_is_Scrapped_139-1"><a href="#cite_note-Karzai_Gets_New_Term_as_Afghan_Runoff_is_Scrapped-139">[138]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Afghan_parliamentary_election,_2005" title="Afghan parliamentary election, 2005">2005 parliamentary election</a>, among the elected officials were former mujahideen, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic_fundamentalists" title="Islamic fundamentalists">Islamic fundamentalists</a>, warlords, communists, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reformists" title="Reformists">reformists</a>, and several Taliban associates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup> In the same period, Afghanistan reached to the 30th highest nation in terms of female representation in parliament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup> The last <a href="/wiki/Afghan_parliamentary_election,_2010" title="Afghan parliamentary election, 2010">parliamentary election</a> was held in September 2010, but due to disputes and investigation of fraud, the swearing-in ceremony took place in late January 2011. The <a href="/wiki/Afghan_presidential_election,_2014" title="Afghan presidential election, 2014">2014 presidential election</a> ended with Ashraf Ghani winning by 56.44% votes.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Afghanistan" title="Provinces of Afghanistan">Provinces of Afghanistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Afghanistan" title="Districts of Afghanistan">Districts of Afghanistan</a></div>
<p>Afghanistan is administratively divided into 34 provinces (<i><a href="/wiki/Wilayah" title="Wilayah">wilayats</a></i>), with each province having its own capital and a provincial administration. The provinces are further divided into about 398 smaller provincial districts, each of which normally covers a city or a number of villages. Each district is represented by a district governor.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_current_governors_of_Afghanistan" title="List of current governors of Afghanistan">provincial governors</a> are appointed by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Afghanistan" title="President of Afghanistan">President of Afghanistan</a> and the district governors are selected by the provincial governors. The provincial governors are representatives of the central government in Kabul and are responsible for all administrative and formal issues within their provinces. There are also provincial councils that are elected through direct and general elections for a period of four years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup> The functions of provincial councils are to take part in provincial development planning and to participate in the monitoring and appraisal of other provincial governance institutions.</p>
<p>According to article 140 of the constitution and the presidential decree on electoral law, mayors of cities should be elected through free and direct elections for a four-year term. However, due to huge election costs, mayoral and municipal elections have never been held. Instead, mayors have been appointed by the government. In the capital city of Kabul, the mayor is appointed by the President of Afghanistan.</p>
<p>The following is a list of all the 34 provinces in alphabetical order:</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
